              <span id="reviewTextContainer2984997415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15362037918054415569">Definitely another higher ranked 3.5! By some happy accident i decided to read the introductory author's note, which i for some reason very rarely bother to do (i think maybe i don't want the author to say anything that will influence how i go into the story). But it is lucky i did because for some reason Clarke decided this book was to be a sequel to the movie, not the first book???? I'm not sure... who would watch the movie and decide to read the second book without reading the first book but </span>
  <span id="freeText15362037918054415569" style="display:none">Definitely another higher ranked 3.5! By some happy accident i decided to read the introductory author's note, which i for some reason very rarely bother to do (i think maybe i don't want the author to say anything that will influence how i go into the story). But it is lucky i did because for some reason Clarke decided this book was to be a sequel to the movie, not the first book???? I'm not sure... who would watch the movie and decide to read the second book without reading the first book but maybe that's not as odd a decision as i feel it is. By the end of this book i think i can see why Clarke did it though. I suspect he felt the direction he wanted to take the story in would better build on the choices of the movie than the book. It's kind of an uncommon blessing for an author to be able to make decisions about his sequel without being bound to the decisions he made for the first installment LOL. Although i am still confused about why the differences between the first book/movie exist if they were written concurrently. I am just confused about so many things sjfkdgjdl but i am really really enjoying the cosmic mystery that is unfolding in this series and can't wait to learn more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15362037918054415569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2448091394" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448091394" />
    <a title="Ravindu Gamage" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16081290-ravindu-gamage"><img alt="Ravindu Gamage" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528202498p2/16081290.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2448091394?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ravindu Gamage" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ravindu Gamage" href="/user/show/16081290-ravindu-gamage">Ravindu Gamage</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345303066" href="/book/show/414967.2010">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2448091394" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5505628322566345758">Let's get the gripes out of the way. <br/><br/>The setting of this sequel has been changed to match the setting of the film and it bothered me throughout the book. While I understand why it might have been done, I'd have preferred if Clarke stayed true to his first book rather than trying to write a sequel to the movie. <br/><br/>As I said <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437295625?book_show_action=false&from_review_page=1' rel='nofollow noopener'>in my review of 2001,</a> I found the lack of character development refreshing. Clarke was more focused on the science rather than the characters. In this book, I found that not to b</span>
  <span id="freeText5505628322566345758" style="display:none">Let's get the gripes out of the way. <br /><br />The setting of this sequel has been changed to match the setting of the film and it bothered me throughout the book. While I understand why it might have been done, I'd have preferred if Clarke stayed true to his first book rather than trying to write a sequel to the movie. <br /><br />As I said <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437295625?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">in my review of 2001,</a> I found the lack of character development refreshing. Clarke was more focused on the science rather than the characters. In this book, I found that not to be true given that the focus of the first part of the book was given to the family and personal lives of the characters rather than the Sci-Fi aspect of the story. <br /><br />That being said, this is still a great book. Not as good as the first, but good enough to warrant 4/5 stars. The story was beautiful and provided explanations for the cliffhangers from the last book, up to a certain extent. Just like the first, this also never felt boring or stagnant. I would definitely continue to read the series and see where Clarke takes this story to. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5505628322566345758" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3367654652" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3367654652" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/99936350-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573532272p2/99936350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3367654652?book_show_action=true">May 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/99936350-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3367654652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12181525954925789843">This is a classic case of diminishing returns on a series which probably never needed a sequel but got several. I'm looking at you Matrix films. <br/><br/>2001 was a fantastic read full of mystery and the sense that for all intents and purposes, we had interacted with an alien intelligence and technology that was so far advanced that it may as well be magic. <br/><br/>This book starts to deconstruct all that and bring the story back down to Earth but not in a particularly personal or intimate way that might have wo</span>
  <span id="freeText12181525954925789843" style="display:none">This is a classic case of diminishing returns on a series which probably never needed a sequel but got several. I'm looking at you Matrix films. <br /><br />2001 was a fantastic read full of mystery and the sense that for all intents and purposes, we had interacted with an alien intelligence and technology that was so far advanced that it may as well be magic. <br /><br />This book starts to deconstruct all that and bring the story back down to Earth but not in a particularly personal or intimate way that might have worked more effectively. It was more in a fashion of over explaining the mystical elements of this ancient system put in place by mysterious alien race or races and introducing just, well, smaller ideas. <br /><br />No I'm probably underselling this book- it's good and "medium" Arthur Clarke can still be formidable and read worthy but it's just that I never minded the open ended question mark kind of end to the first book that left me thinking about huge concepts of alien intelligence and contact.<br /><br />It's closer to 3.5 stars but that's about it given how good the first book is. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12181525954925789843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eDueFRvqn42m/yN5GxqquU7JbbDd5C9CqefLKQXlhbGMGJSrEjCMRD6ghc87rlGUN3x1YxsfAB5hUBd1R9ay4w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18065037352027555711">Arthur Charles Clarke was one of the most important and influential figures in 20th century science fiction. He spent the first half of his life in England, where he served in World War Two as a radar operator, before emigrating to Ceylon in 1956. He is best known for the novel and movie <i>2001: A Space Odyssey</i>, which he co-created with the assistance of Stanley Kubrick.<br/><br/>Clarke was a graduate of King</span>
  <span id="freeText18065037352027555711" style="display:none">Arthur Charles Clarke was one of the most important and influential figures in 20th century science fiction. He spent the first half of his life in England, where he served in World War Two as a radar operator, before emigrating to Ceylon in 1956. He is best known for the novel and movie <i>2001: A Space Odyssey</i>, which he co-created with the assistance of Stanley Kubrick.<br /><br />Clarke was a graduate of King's College, London where he obtained First Class Honours in Physics and Mathematics. He is past Chairman of the British Interplanetary Society, a member of the Academy of Astronautics, the Royal Astronomical Society, and many other scientific organizations.<br /><br />Author of over fifty books, his numerous awards include the 1961 Kalinga Prize, the AAAS-Westinghouse science writing prize, the Bradford Washburn Award, and the John W. Campbell Award for his novel <i>Rendezvous With Rama</i>. Clarke also won the Nebula Award of the Science Fiction Writers of America in 1972, 1974 and 1979, the Hugo Award of the World Science Fiction Convention in 1974 and 1980, and in 1986 became Grand Master of the Science Fiction Writers of America. He was awarded the CBE in 1989.</span>
